# NBAgent — Roadmap: Resolved Issues

All resolved bugs, completed improvements, and closed hypotheses. See `docs/ROADMAP_active.md` for the active queue and `docs/BACKTESTS.md` for backtest details.

---

| Issue | Fix Applied |
|-------|-------------|
| **Miss Classification Analysis v2 — picks.json enrichment + confidence-band analysis + tightened keyword detection (2026-05-01)** | Extended `tools/miss_classification.py` with three v2 enrichments. **(1) picks.json join** via the unique `(date, player_name, prop_type, pick_value)` key (verified 1337/1337 unique on full picks.json). New helpers: `load_picks_lookup()` (returns dict for enrichment, includes voided/ungraded/graded picks) and `load_picks_baseline()` (returns DataFrame of graded HIT|MISS picks with `voided=false`, the rate denominator for v2). New row enrichment fields on each miss: `confidence_pct`, `confidence_band` (categorical: `70_74` / `75_79` / `80_84` / `85_89` / `90_plus`; <70 → null graceful), `market_implied_prob`, `is_high_conviction` (bool ≥85). Unmatched-row warning: graceful console log + null fields. **(2) New Section 5a — Confidence Band Analysis** with three sub-tables: 5a.1 pick volume by band (incl. expected hit rate from band midpoint, overshoot pp = actual − expected), 5a.2 miss classification breakdown within each band (n<5 → insufficient-sample placeholder), 5a.3 razor-margin variance concentration by band. Section 5a.1 includes an `<70 (unbanded)` row + TOTAL row so the column-total matches the graded-baseline invariant exactly (3 picks with confidence_pct < 70 surface as the unbanded population). **Section 5 (Prop-Type Concentration) modified** — now takes `baseline` parameter, adds `total picks (graded)` and `miss rate %` columns. **Section 6 (Player Concentration) modified** — adds `total_picks` and `miss rate %` columns from baseline; dossier-candidate flag tightened from pure miss-count threshold to BOTH `total_misses >= 5` AND `miss_rate_pct >= 15%` so high-volume players with average miss rates are NOT flagged. **Section 9 (Findings) modified** — adds two new diagnostic subsections after the calibration check: "Confidence band overshoot diagnostic" (per-band overshoot + razor-variance share + framing for whether the lowest band's overshoot is concentrated in razor variance, the central recalibration question) and "Per-prop miss rate diagnostic" (flags any prop whose miss rate is >1.5× the lowest-rate prop). **(3) Tightened keyword detection** — `KEYWORD_PATTERNS` rewritten with causal-phrase variants (active phrasing implying causal attribution, not mere mention) plus 30-character negation lookback in `detect_keywords()`. New negation markers: `no `, `not `, `without `, `never `, `absent`, `isn't`, `wasn't`, `didn't`. Two new pattern groups added to v1's 12: `near_miss_variance` (missed by exactly 1/2, near-miss) and `structural_ceiling` (ceiling miss, well below the threshold) — these pair directly with the miss margin distribution data. **Verification (all 12 invariants + idempotency pass):** (1) Section 5a.1 row sum = 1215 = graded baseline; (2) hits + misses = picks per band; (3) hit_rate × total ≈ hits within ±1; (4) total miss rows preserved at 172; (5) per-prop miss-rate × picks ≈ misses within ±1; (6) dossier flags satisfy AND condition (verified no false positives or missed flags); (7) section ordering 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 5a, 6, 7, 8, 9 preserved (5a inserted between 5 and 6); (8) byte-identical md5 across two runs (idempotent); (9) **negation guard observable effect — `blowout` keyword in `model_gap_rule` dropped from v1's 88.1% (52/59) to v2's 18.6% (11/59) — a ~80% reduction**, confirming the auditor's "No blowout context" boilerplate is now correctly suppressed; (10) console output `[miss_classification] Wrote {path} (172 miss rows analyzed)` unchanged; (11) sparse confidence bands (`85_89` n=2, `90_plus` n=0) correctly show `_(insufficient sample, n=N)_` placeholder in 5a.2; (12) `workflow_gap` n=6 and `selection_error` n=5 both apply the v1 n≥5 graceful behavior — workflow_gap attempts detection and finds 0 v2 matches (honest answer; v1 found false positives via loose substrings like "limited minutes" that v2 correctly suppresses). **Headline v2 findings on first run** (172 miss rows, 1215 graded picks baseline): the **70_74 band has the largest overshoot (+13.4pp on 512 picks, 85.9% actual vs 72.5% expected)** — strongest calibration signal in the dataset. AST surfaces in the per-prop diagnostic with elevated miss rate. Donovan Mitchell (10 misses on 27 picks = 37.0% miss rate) and Derrick White (9 misses on 25 picks = 36.0% miss rate) both flag as dossier-review candidates under the tightened AND criterion. The `blowout` v1 finding (88% in model_gap_rule) is now correctly identified as keyword-inflated; the v2 causal rate (18.6%) is the honest signal. **Files touched:** `tools/miss_classification.py` (modified — v1 structure preserved, v2 sections added in-place), `data/miss_classification_report.md` (regenerated, same path, enriched content). **Not touched:** `agents/auditor.py` (the keyword tightening responds to auditor boilerplate phrasing but the fix lives in the analyzer; changing auditor output would invalidate historical audit_log data), all other agent files, all `ingest/*.py`, all `.github/workflows/*.yml`, all data files (read-only access to `audit_log.json` and `picks.json` only), `context/nba_season_context.md`, `docs/AGENTS.md`, `docs/DATA.md` (no schema changes; report file path unchanged), `CLAUDE.md`. **Recommended downstream work:** review report Section 5a.3 razor-variance share within the 70_74 band; if the share is >50%, confidence recalibration is the highest-leverage next workstream; otherwise the diagnosis is more nuanced and other workstreams (Mitchell/White dossier expansion, AST tier rule review) should also be considered. Per project discipline, any rule candidate named in the report still requires its own backtest before shipping. |
| **Miss Classification Analysis Tool (2026-05-01)** | New standalone read-only research script `tools/miss_classification.py` — descriptive analysis over `data/audit_log.json`. Output: `data/miss_classification_report.md`. **Decision input for next major workstream choice (multi-agent expert architecture vs new data pipelines vs rule additions vs calibration recalibration). Not a directive — no rules ship from this report.** **9 sections:** (1) Overview — date range 2026-03-04 → 2026-04-30, 55 audit entries, 172 miss rows analyzed (179 raw - 7 null-classified excluded), `model_gap` (legacy alias) and `model_gap_signal` bucketed identically as `catchable_with_new_data` but reported separately so audit-time taxonomy drift remains visible; (2) Taxonomy Breakdown — 7-class table (variance 39.5%, model_gap_rule 34.3%, model_gap_signal 7.0%, model_gap 7.0%, injury_event 5.8%, workflow_gap 3.5%, selection_error 2.9%); (3) Four-Bucket Roll-up — inherent_variance 45.3%, deterministic_rule_catchable 37.8%, catchable_with_new_data 14.0%, catchable_with_current_signals 2.9%; (4) Keyword Pattern Frequency Within Each Classification — case-insensitive substring matching against `root_cause` text using 12 pattern groups (blowout, fg_margin_thin, fg_cold, suppressor_cross_prop, foul_trouble, injury_exit, rebounding_competition, minutes_compression, h2h_thin, tier_walk_market, playoff_intensity, volatile_tag); top-5 patterns per class with n≥5; classes with n<5 render `_(insufficient sample, n=N)_` placeholder; (5) Prop-Type Concentration — per-prop counts + top-3 classifications; (6) Player Concentration — top-10 players + flag for >5% share (Donovan Mitchell 10 misses 5.8% and Derrick White 9 misses 5.2% surface as dossier-review candidates); (7) Miss Margin Distribution — mean/median/p25/p75/max + razor (≤1) / small (2-3) / medium (4-6) / large (7+) buckets per classification; (8) Regular-Season vs Playoff Split — date < 2026-04-18 vs date ≥; flags >5pp divergence; (9) Findings & Workstream Recommendation — non-directive synthesis identifying largest catchable bucket, top-3 patterns within each actionable bucket, single-pick concentration, calibration check (`variance` 45.3% with 85.3% razor/small margins → suggests calibration is the dominant lever), and one explicit open question for human review. **Stack:** Python stdlib + pandas, single file ~470 lines, no new dependencies. Reads only `data/audit_log.json` (read-only); writes only `data/miss_classification_report.md`. **Idempotent** — running twice produces byte-identical output (audit-log date range is the version anchor; no clock-time stamps in body). Console output: `[miss_classification] Wrote {path} (172 miss rows analyzed)`. **Verification (all 6 mathematical invariants + idempotency check pass):** (1) 7-class counts sum to 172; (2) 4-bucket counts sum to 172 (matches by construction); (3) `model_gap` + `model_gap_signal` (12+12=24) = `catchable_with_new_data` (24); (4) `model_gap_rule` + `workflow_gap` (59+6=65) = `deterministic_rule_catchable` (65); (5) prop-type counts sum to 172; (6) all 9 section headers present; (7) re-run produces byte-identical md5 hash. Empty-class behavior verified: `selection_error` n=5 sits at the threshold and renders the pattern table (threshold is `n < 5`). **Headline finding:** the largest catchable bucket is `deterministic_rule_catchable` (69% of catchable population, top pattern `blowout` 52 matches), but the calibration-check trigger fires (`variance` 45% of total, 85% razor/small margins) — suggesting the *next* workstream may be calibration recalibration rather than blowout rule expansion. The report explicitly does not prescribe; the open question is "blowout-rule expansion, or accept that variance and prioritize the next-largest bucket?" — answered in an offseason planning conversation, not by this prompt's execution. **Files touched:** `tools/miss_classification.py` (NEW), `data/miss_classification_report.md` (NEW). **Not touched:** `agents/auditor.py` (the legacy `model_gap` taxonomy value is reported separately for transparency, not normalized away — auditor classification logic untouched), `agents/analyst.py`, `agents/quant.py`, `agents/parlay.py`, `agents/backtest.py` (this is NOT a backtest mode — no `--mode` added, no `backtest_*.json` artifact), `agents/build_site.py`, all other agent files, all `ingest/*.py`, all `.github/workflows/*.yml`, `data/picks.json`, `data/audit_log.json` (read-only), `data/audit_summary.json`, `data/skipped_picks.json`, `data/player_stats.json`, `context/nba_season_context.md`, `CLAUDE.md`. **Recommended downstream work:** review the report's section 9 with the user; choose next workstream from the candidate areas surfaced (calibration recalibration / blowout rule expansion / Donovan Mitchell + Derrick White dossier deep-dive / multi-agent expert architecture). Per project discipline, any rule candidate named in the report requires its own backtest before shipping — the report describes patterns, it does not prescribe. |
| **MARKET_GATE_REJECT structured logging shipped (2026-05-01)** | `agents/analyst.py` only — closes the structured-logging companion to the 2026-04-26 tier walk market-awareness fix. **Three-part change:** (1) `enforce_market_gate()` signature changed from `-> list[dict]` to `-> tuple[list[dict], list[dict]]`. The function now constructs a skip-shaped dict for each pick it rejects (instead of just incrementing a counter). New `skip_reason: "market_gate_reject"` value with `rule_context.failure_mode` in `{player_absent, tier_absent}`. For `player_absent` (player not in FanDuel `odds_available.json` data at all), `rule_context.available_tiers = None`. For `tier_absent` (player exists but pick's tier not in the prop's tier ladder), `rule_context.available_tiers` is a sorted list of integer tiers that DID exist for that player+prop. Both gate-disabled paths (file missing/stale OR `players_markets` empty) return `(picks, [])` so the unpack signature is consistent across all 5 return paths. (2) `save_picks()` signature changed from `-> list[dict]` (implicit) to `-> tuple[list[dict], list[dict]]` with explicit return type annotation and updated docstring. The body unpacks `enforce_market_gate()`'s tuple return into `picks, market_gate_rejections` and surfaces the rejections back to the caller in the final return. Picks.json write contract is unchanged — rejections do NOT go into picks.json. The post-processor chain order (`filter_self_skip_picks → reconcile_pick_values → revert_no_market_walk → reconcile_game_attribution → enforce_market_gate → compute_observability → write`) is unchanged. (3) **Four `main()` call sites** updated to thread the rejections through to `save_skips()`: three fallback paths (Scout returns no picks / undersized Scout shortlist / fewer than 5 shortlisted players match quant) and one normal-path call after the Pick stage. Canonical pattern at all four sites: `picks, market_gate_rejections = save_picks(picks, player_stats); save_skips(skips + market_gate_rejections)`. List concatenation order is LLM skips first, then Python rejections — preserves chronological emission order. **`save_skips()` itself is unchanged** — it still adds the four nullable grading fields (`actual_value`, `would_have_hit`, `skip_verdict`, `skip_verdict_notes`) automatically, so rejected records inherit the same auditor grading lifecycle as LLM skips. **LLM-visible `skip_reason` enum unchanged** in `build_prompt()` and `build_pick_prompt()` — the new `market_gate_reject` value is exclusively Python-emitted. Adding it to the LLM-facing enum would risk confusing the LLM into emitting it when violating the gate (the correct LLM response remains `skip_reason: "no_market"` when it detects no market itself; `market_gate_reject` is what fires when the LLM violates the gate and Python catches it). **Console-log format unchanged** — the existing `[analyst] MARKET_GATE_REJECT: <player> <prop> T<tier> — <reason>` log line stays exactly as before. The new structured logging is purely additive — every console line now has a parallel structured record in `skipped_picks.json`. **Verification (all 7 grep gates pass):** `def enforce_market_gate(picks: list[dict]) -> tuple[list[dict], list[dict]]:` = 1; `def save_picks(picks: list[dict], player_stats: dict | None = None) -> tuple[list[dict], list[dict]]:` = 1; `picks, market_gate_rejections = save_picks` = 4 (one per call site); `save_skips(skips + market_gate_rejections)` = 4; `^    picks = save_picks(` = 0 (no lingering 4-space old form); `^        picks = save_picks(` = 0 (no lingering 8-space old form); `save_skips\(skips\)$` = 0 (no lingering unmerged save_skips). Python `ast.parse` clean. **Functional smoke test (synthetic picks with stubbed `load_available_markets`):** kept count = 1 (LeBron PTS T15 in market), rejected count = 2 (Ghost Player → player_absent with `available_tiers: null`; LeBron PTS T25 → tier_absent with `available_tiers: [15, 20]`); all 9 schema invariants pass on each rejected record (required top-level fields present, `skip_reason == "market_gate_reject"`, `direction == "OVER"`, `failure_mode` in expected set, `available_tiers` shape correct per failure_mode, rejected tier NOT in available list, rejected records do NOT pre-populate the four nullable grading fields — `save_skips()` adds them); gate-disabled paths return `(picks, [])` correctly; `save_skips()` integration confirmed — merged LLM skip + 2 market_gate_reject records all written with the four nullable grading fields filled. **Files touched:** `agents/analyst.py` only — 3 edits (enforce_market_gate body + signature, save_picks signature + return, all 4 call sites updated via 1 `replace_all` for the 3 byte-identical fallback patterns + 1 unique edit for the normal path). **Not touched:** `save_skips()` (still adds the four nullable fields automatically), `filter_self_skip_picks`, `reconcile_pick_values`, `revert_no_market_walk`, `reconcile_game_attribution`, `compute_observability`, the picks.json write contract, the `[analyst] MARKET_GATE_REJECT:` console log format, the LLM-visible `skip_reason` enum strings in `build_prompt()` / `build_pick_prompt()` (lines ~3244 / ~4598), `agents/auditor.py` (the auditor grades `market_gate_reject` and `no_market` skip records via the same code path — they're both "we couldn't have bet this anyway"), `agents/build_site.py` (skip-reason rendering is value-agnostic), all other agent files, all `ingest/*.py`, all `.github/workflows/*.yml`, `data/picks.json` schema, `data/skipped_picks.json` schema (the new value flows through the existing schema unchanged). **Recommended downstream work** (queued in `ROADMAP_active.md` as W12): on the next analyst run that produces a gate violation, verify the 1:1 console-line ↔ structured-record parity and the `failure_mode` / `available_tiers` shape. Auditor verdict-text awareness of the new `skip_reason` value is deferred — current grading collapses both `no_market` and `market_gate_reject` into "couldn't bet anyway", which is correct; if a follow-up reveals the auditor needs explicit verdict-text differentiation, that's a separate prompt. |
| **Kalshi P4 frontend toggle live (2026-05-01)** | `agents/build_site.py` only — single-file change, no ingest or schema changes. Adds a "Kalshi-listed only" toggle below the existing High-conviction toggle on the Today's Picks tab. Filter composes with the HC toggle via logical AND: a card is shown iff it passes EVERY active filter. **Three implementation parts:** (1) **Per-card `data-kalshi` attribute** added in all three pick-card render functions (`renderPicks`, `renderTopPicks`, `renderBestBets`) alongside the existing `data-hc` attribute. New local `kalshiAttr` derivation: `(p.kalshi_market_listed === true) ? 'true' : 'false'` — strict `=== true` comparison so anything other than literal `true` (false, undefined, null, missing field on legacy pre-P1 picks) resolves to `'false'`. (2) **Toggle UI markup** — new `<div class="high-conv-toggle-wrap">` with `id="kalshi-toggle"` checkbox + `id="kalshi-counter"` span placed immediately below the existing HC toggle inside `<div id="tab-picks">`. The wrapper class `high-conv-toggle-wrap` is intentionally re-used as a layout chassis (its CSS is layout-only — flex row, padding, border, radius); ditto `hc-toggle-label` and `hc-toggle-counter`. Renaming the historical class would ripple through CSS and existing state and is out of scope. New CSS rule: `.high-conv-toggle-wrap + .high-conv-toggle-wrap {{ margin-top: 8px; }}` — adjacent-sibling combinator gives 8px gap between two stacked wraps; rule has zero effect on a single isolated wrap. Label text is `"Kalshi-listed only"` (terse, parallel form to HC's `"High-conviction only (market ≥ 85%)"` but without the threshold parenthetical since Kalshi listing is binary, not a threshold). (3) **Filter IIFE replaced with unified `applyAllFilters()` handler** — original `applyHCFilter` IIFE could not coexist with a parallel Kalshi IIFE because each filter writes to `card.style.display` independently and would un-hide what the other just hid. The unified handler reads BOTH toggles and composes them via logical AND: `passHC = !hcOn || card.dataset.hc === 'true'`; `passKalshi = !kalshiOn || card.dataset.kalshi === 'true'`; `show = passHC && passKalshi`. **Behavioral preservation when only HC is active:** identical to pre-P4 — same set of cards visible/hidden, same game-group collapse, same Top Picks / Best Bets header hiding, same counter message. **Canonical-counter dedup preserved** (session entry 93, 2026-04-25): visibility loop walks ALL `.pick-card` elements (including Top Picks / Best Bets duplicates) so duplicates hide correctly; counter loop walks ONLY `.pick-card[data-canonical="true"]` so duplicates aren't counted. Note: the spec's reference IIFE used a single-loop pattern that would have inflated the counter; deviated from spec to preserve the existing dedup behavior. **Both counters show the same `"Showing X of Y picks"` message when ANY filter is active**; both blank otherwise. Game-group containers, Top Picks header/grid/divider, Best Bets header/grid/divider all hide when their visible card set is empty AND `anyOn = hcOn || kalshiOn`. **In-memory only** — both toggles reset to OFF on page reload (no localStorage persistence, same as pre-P4 HC behavior). **Auditor coverage warning intentionally dropped** — original P4 scope included a "<50% Kalshi coverage" warning, but Kalshi has structurally fewer tiers than FanDuel (e.g. PTS ladder may have only 3-5 Kalshi tiers vs FanDuel's full 5-tier menu), so low coverage days are expected and not a system health signal. No auditor change, no `audit_summary` field, no coverage rollup. **No per-pick "Kalshi" badge added** — the two book lines from P2 (`FanDuel: -150 (60.0%)` / `Kalshi: —`) already show Kalshi presence visually; a badge would be redundant. **Verification (all 8 grep gates pass):** `id="kalshi-toggle"` = 1, `id="kalshi-counter"` = 1, `data-kalshi="${{kalshiAttr}}"` = 3 (one per render function), `const kalshiAttr =` = 3, `.high-conv-toggle-wrap + .high-conv-toggle-wrap` = 1, `function applyHCFilter` = 0 (replaced), `function applyAllFilters` = 1 (new unified handler), `kalshiToggle.addEventListener` = 1. Python `ast.parse` clean; `python3 agents/build_site.py` runs cleanly producing `site/index.html` (0 today's picks for 2026-05-01 — analyst hasn't generated picks yet); rendered HTML contains all expected DOM elements (1× kalshi-toggle input, 1× kalshi-counter span, 4× applyAllFilters refs in the JS source). **Files touched:** `agents/build_site.py` only. **Not touched:** existing `data-hc` attribute or its derivation, `.high-conv-toggle-wrap` / `.toggle-switch` / `.slider` / `.hc-toggle-label` / `.hc-toggle-counter` CSS rules (intentionally re-used by new toggle), `buildEdgeLine`, `buildFanDuelLine`, `buildKalshiLine`, `displayConf`, `buildOddsSizing`, `buildMovementLine`, `buildClvWarnBadge`, `buildHitRate`, `buildMicroStats`, `tierLabelFromEdge`, `renderInjuries`, `renderResults`, `renderAudit`, `renderResearch`, parlay leg display (parlay UI unchanged), high-conviction badge logic, voided-pick styling, lineup_update arrow badge, CLV warn badge, line movement indicator, `.book-line` styles. **Not touched:** `ingest/kalshi_today.py`, `ingest/odds_today.py`, all other `ingest/*.py`, all agent files (analyst/auditor/parlay/quant/lineup_watch/lineup_update/pre_game_reporter/post_game_reporter/playoff_matchup/injury_profiles/season_context_updater/backtest), all `.github/workflows/*.yml`, `data/picks.json` schema (fields read, not modified), `context/nba_season_context.md`, `docs/DATA.md`, `docs/AGENTS.md` (no build_site.py section to update), `docs/BACKTESTS.md`, `docs/ROADMAP_Offseason.md`, `CLAUDE.md`. **Recommended downstream work** (queued in `ROADMAP_active.md`): W11 verifies first-render filter composition + counter behavior + page reload reset on next site rebuild with real Kalshi data. P3 (Kalshi disagreement backtest) remains deferred until 5+ slates of Kalshi data accumulate. |
| **Kalshi P2 frontend display live (2026-05-01)** | `agents/build_site.py` only — single-file change, ingest schema unchanged. Three new JS helpers added immediately above `buildEdgeLine`: (1) `impliedToAmerican(impliedPct)` converts implied probability in percent (0–100) to formatted American odds string ("+150" / "-150"); returns `null` for out-of-range inputs (`null`, `<= 0`, `>= 100`). Formula: `raw = -100 * p / (100 - p)` for p ≥ 50, `raw = 100 * (100 - p) / p` for p < 50; `Math.round` then formatted with explicit sign. (2) `buildFanDuelLine(p)` reads `p.market_implied_prob` (FanDuel) and renders `<div class="book-line"><span class="book-label">FanDuel:</span> -150 (60.0%)</div>` in the right rail; defensive `"FanDuel: —"` when `market_implied_prob` is null (rare given Phase 1.5 market gate but handled). (3) `buildKalshiLine(p)` reads `p.kalshi_market_listed` and `p.kalshi_market_implied_prob` (P1 fields) and renders `Kalshi: -135 (57.4%)`; renders `"Kalshi: —"` for three states — `kalshi_market_listed === false` (P1 ingest ran, Kalshi has no market for this player+prop+tier), `kalshi_market_listed === undefined` (legacy picks predating 2026-05-01 P1 ingest), or field present but `kalshi_market_implied_prob` null (partial fetch). New `.book-line` CSS class added immediately after `.edge-line.fade`: 10px monospace, `var(--muted)` base color, 4px top margin matching `.edge-line`, `white-space: nowrap`. Inner `.book-line .book-label` is `var(--text)` bold for label emphasis. Monospace family is intentional — keeps American-odds numbers (e.g. `-150` and `-135`) column-aligned across the FanDuel/Kalshi rows so divergence reads at a glance. **Wired at three render sites** between the `displayConf` line and the existing edge display: (a) `renderPicks()` (Today's Picks rail, after `<div class="conf-line">`), (b) `renderTopPicks()` (Top Picks rail, after `<div class="tp-conf">`), (c) `renderBestBets()` (Best Bets rail, after `<div class="tp-conf">`, before `${{buildEdgeLine(p)}}` — note: spec referenced legacy `bb-edge` div, but Best Bets was migrated to `buildEdgeLine` on 2026-04-25 per session entry 90; insertion point is logically equivalent). All three render points get the same two new lines (FanDuel first, Kalshi second). **No computed delta** between books — visual divergence read at a glance. **`buildEdgeLine`, `bb-edge`, and `displayConf` unchanged** — edge label remains FanDuel-derived. **No new field added to `picks.json`** — P2 is rendering only. **Verification (all gates pass):** Python `ast.parse` clean; spec grep matrix exact — `function impliedToAmerican` = 1, `function buildFanDuelLine` = 1, `function buildKalshiLine` = 1, `buildFanDuelLine(p)` = 4 (1 def + 3 calls), `buildKalshiLine(p)` = 4 (1 def + 3 calls), `\.book-line` = 2 (selector + `.book-label` selector), `function buildEdgeLine` = 1 (unchanged), `tierLabelFromEdge` = 2 (unchanged); `python3 agents/build_site.py` runs cleanly producing `site/index.html` (0 today's picks for 2026-05-01 expected — analyst hasn't generated picks yet); 8/9 mathematical sanity assertions on `impliedToAmerican` pass — 52.38% → -110, 60% → -150, 40% → +150, 80% → -400, all out-of-range inputs return null; the spec's `impliedToAmerican(50) === '+100'` test case is inconsistent with the spec's own helper code (formula at p=50 yields `raw = -100`, output = `"-100"`, mathematically equivalent to `+100` since both represent even money). **Files touched:** `agents/build_site.py` only. **Not touched:** `ingest/kalshi_today.py`, `ingest/odds_today.py`, all other `ingest/*.py`, all agent files (`analyst`, `auditor`, `parlay`, `quant`, `lineup_watch`, `lineup_update`, `pre_game_reporter`, `post_game_reporter`, `playoff_matchup`, `injury_profiles`, `season_context_updater`, `backtest`), all `.github/workflows/*.yml`, `data/picks.json` schema (fields read, not modified), `context/nba_season_context.md`, `docs/DATA.md`, `docs/AGENTS.md` (no build_site.py section to update), `docs/BACKTESTS.md`, `docs/ROADMAP_Offseason.md`, `CLAUDE.md`. **Not touched within `build_site.py`:** `buildEdgeLine`, `tierLabelFromEdge`, `displayConf`, `buildOddsSizing`, `buildMovementLine`, `buildHitRate`, `buildMicroStats`, `buildClvWarnBadge`, `applyHCFilter`, `renderInjuries`, `renderResults`, `renderAudit`, `renderResearch`, parlay leg display (lines ~3130 / 3189 / 3315 — parlay UI is unchanged in P2 per scope), high-conviction badge logic, voided-pick styling, lineup_update arrow badge, CLV warn badge, line movement indicator, `data-canonical` attribute, HC counter, `.conf-line` / `.edge-line` / `.bb-edge` styles. **Recommended downstream work** (queued in `ROADMAP_active.md`): W10 verifies first-render coverage matrix on next site rebuild with real Kalshi data; P3 (Kalshi disagreement backtest at `--mode kalshi-disagreement` in `agents/backtest.py`) remains deferred until 5+ slates of Kalshi data accumulate (target ≥2026-05-06). Future Kalshi-aware edge logic (e.g. flagging large FanDuel-Kalshi disagreements with color treatment) is a separate prompt — P2 ships visual side-by-side display only. |
| **Kalshi P1 ingest mirror live (2026-05-01)** | New `ingest/kalshi_today.py` mirrors the FanDuel `ingest/odds_today.py` pipeline architecturally with two modes (`main()` morning capture + `--pretip` hourly refresh), but targets Kalshi's public Markets API at `api.elections.kalshi.com/trade-api/v2/`. **Pure stdlib only** — `urllib.request` + `urllib.parse` + `urllib.error`, no `requests` dependency, no API key (Kalshi public endpoint), no auth, GET-only. **Same polite-throttle posture as the kalshi probes:** `THROTTLE_SEC = 0.20`, `PAGE_LIMIT = 200`, `MAX_PAGES = 10`, `User-Agent: NBAgent-KalshiIngest/1.0`. **Four series targeted** per the v2 reprobe finding: `KXNBAPTS` → PTS, `KXNBAREB` → REB, `KXNBAAST` → AST, `KXNBA3PT` → 3PM (note Kalshi's 3PT vs NBAgent's 3PM convention). **Per-pick `kalshi_*` namespace added to `picks.json`:** nine new fields — `kalshi_market_listed` (bool, set on every pickable today's pick by `main()` only — `pretip_sweep()` does NOT flip false→true), `kalshi_market_ticker` (full Kalshi ticker like `KXNBAPTS-26MAY01CLETOR-DM1-15`), `kalshi_yes_bid_dollars` (top-of-book YES bid 0–1), `kalshi_yes_ask_dollars` (top-of-book YES ask 0–1), `kalshi_market_implied_prob` (= `yes_bid_dollars × 100`, in PERCENT to match FanDuel's `market_implied_prob` convention so future P3 CLV math can subtract directly), `kalshi_morning_implied_prob` (first-capture baseline frozen for CLV; set once per pick per day, never overwritten — sticky across pretip refreshes), `kalshi_volume_24h_fp` (Kalshi 24h trade volume in contracts, refreshed each cycle), `kalshi_settlement_rule` (always `"last_fair_price"` — Kalshi binary contracts settle to last fair market price on DNP-active scratches; FanDuel voids in the same scenario, so the auditor's future P5 reconciliation logic needs to know which rule fired), `kalshi_fetched_at` (ISO timestamp). All `kalshi_*` fields are independent of and additive to FanDuel `market_*` / `morning_implied_prob` fields — no namespace collision. **Tip-off guard in `pretip_sweep()`:** reads `nba_master.csv` `game_time_utc` column, builds `commenced_teams` set for today's slate using `PRETIP_GRACE_MINUTES = 30` (mirrors `odds_today.py`), and SKIPS refresh on any pick whose team or opponent has commenced AND already has `kalshi_market_implied_prob` set. This preserves the last pre-tip implied probability as the closing-line anchor for CLV calculations. First-capture-post-tip case allowed but logs a `WARNING: ... CLV may be unreliable` line. **Fallback morning baseline** in `pretip_sweep()` — if a pick has `kalshi_market_listed=true` but `kalshi_morning_implied_prob` was never set (e.g., morning capture missed it because Kalshi hadn't listed the player yet), the first pretip cycle that matches that pick sets `kalshi_morning_implied_prob` from the current implied as a "better-than-nothing" baseline; logged as `FALLBACK MORNING:`. **Meaningful movement logging** — `MOVEMENT:` line printed for any pick where `|new_implied − prior_implied| ≥ 1.0pp`. **Workflow integration:** (1) `analyst.yml` gains a new step `Enrich picks with Kalshi odds` between the existing `Enrich picks with odds` (FanDuel) and `Commit picks` steps; `data/kalshi_today.json` appended to the `FILES=` list. (2) `odds_pretip.yml` gains a new step `Run pre-tip Kalshi sweep` immediately after `Run pre-tip odds sweep` (FanDuel pretip); `data/kalshi_today.json` appended to its `FILES=` list. **Cron schedule unchanged** — Kalshi piggybacks on FanDuel's hourly cadence verbatim. **No prefetch mode** (`--prefetch` exists on `odds_today.py` for the FanDuel market-availability gate; Kalshi is NOT used as a market gate, only annotation, so the prefetch flag would be dead code). **No snapshot file** like `odds_pretip.json` — Kalshi has no API quota so per-hour refreshes are free and need no dedup. The morning baseline lives durably on each pick as `kalshi_morning_implied_prob`. **No liquidity classification** stored — only raw `kalshi_volume_24h_fp` plus bid/ask. The probe's `liquid` / `thin` / `top_of_book` / `empty` buckets are deferred to P2/P3 if needed. **Failure mode is exit 0 with warning** — mirrors `odds_today.py` exactly. The workflow re-runs hourly; transient failures self-heal on the next cron tick. Atomic write via `tmp_path → os.replace()`. **Verification (all gates pass):** Python `ast.parse` clean; stdlib-only confirmed (only `csv`, `datetime`, `json`, `os`, `re`, `sys`, `time`, `pathlib`, `urllib`, `zoneinfo`, `argparse` — no `requests`); 3 unit-style assertions pass — `_slate_date_ticker(dt.date(2026, 5, 1)) == "26MAY01"`, name normalization parity with `odds_today.py` (`"Karl-Anthony Towns"` → `"karlanthony towns"`, `"De'Aaron Fox"` → `"deaaron fox"`, `"Shai Gilgeous-Alexander"` → `"shai gilgeousalexander"`), `parse_market()` on canonical fake correctly returns `ok=True, player="Donovan Mitchell", prop_type="PTS", tier=15`; both YAML files parse cleanly; spec grep matrix passes — `Enrich picks with Kalshi odds` count = 1, `Run pre-tip Kalshi sweep` count = 1, `data/kalshi_today.json` in `analyst.yml` = 1, `data/kalshi_today.json` in `odds_pretip.yml` = 1. **Live morning run** on 2026-05-01 hit the graceful no-op path (`No unvoided pickable picks for 2026-05-01 — skipping`) because today's analyst run hasn't generated picks yet — that's correct behavior, exits 0 before any work. **Live API connectivity check** (read-only, no `picks.json` mutation) against today's slate (`26MAY01`) confirmed Kalshi has all 374 markets pre-listed across the four series for tonight's three matchups (`DETORL`, `CLETOR`, `LALHOU` — Kalshi already had them at the time of the v2 reprobe yesterday); 0 parse failures; sample matched markets show clean shape — `Alperen Sengun AST T2 → KXNBAAST-26MAY01LALHOU-HOUASENGUN28-2: yes_bid=$0.97 v24h=0.0`, `Sengun AST T6: yes_bid=$0.58 v24h=1412.36`, etc. **NBAgent data integrity preserved:** `git status` clean on `picks.json`, `audit_log.json`, `audit_summary.json`, `lineups_today.json`, `injuries_today.json`, `player_stats.json`, `skipped_picks.json`, `parlays.json`. **Files touched:** `ingest/kalshi_today.py` (NEW, ~520 lines), `.github/workflows/analyst.yml` (1 step + 1 file added to FILES list), `.github/workflows/odds_pretip.yml` (1 step + 1 file added to FILES list). **Not touched:** `ingest/odds_today.py` (FanDuel pipeline must remain identical — Kalshi is strictly additive, no shared-helper factor-out), `ingest/espn_daily_ingest.py`, `ingest/espn_player_ingest.py`, `ingest/rotowire_injuries_only.py` (read-only consumer of `nba_master.csv`'s `game_date` / `game_time_utc` / `home_team_abbrev` / `away_team_abbrev` columns), all agents (`analyst.py`, `auditor.py`, `parlay.py`, `build_site.py`, `quant.py`, `lineup_watch.py`, `lineup_update.py`, `pre_game_reporter.py`, `post_game_reporter.py`, `playoff_matchup.py`, `season_context_updater.py`, `injury_profiles.py`, `backtest.py` — Kalshi data is currently invisible to all of them by design), all other `.yml` workflows (`ingest.yml`, `injuries.yml`, `auditor.yml`, `odds.yml`, `diag.yml`, `build_site.yml`), `data/nba_master.csv` schema, `context/nba_season_context.md`. **Recommended downstream work** (queued in `ROADMAP_active.md`): W8 (verify P1 first production run) + W9 (track coverage rate over first 5 slates — below 50% on any slate triggers data investigation, over 80% is healthy); P2 frontend display (side-by-side Kalshi vs FanDuel implied prob on pick cards) and P3 disagreement backtest (new `--mode` in `backtest.py` after 5+ slates of Kalshi data accumulate) both deferred. |
| **Kalshi re-probe v2 — orderbook parsing bugfix (2026-04-30)** | New `tools/kalshi_reprobe_v2.py` corrects two parsing bugs in the v1 re-probe (`tools/kalshi_reprobe.py` shipped earlier the same day). **Bug 1 — outer key:** the orderbook response top-level key is `orderbook_fp`, NOT `orderbook`. The v1 probe walked `ob.get("orderbook")` and got `None`, falling through to empty arrays — that's why v1 reported "0 of 355 markets had any depth" as a parsing artifact, not a real liquidity finding. **Bug 2 — inner keys + value types:** the inner keys are `yes_dollars` / `no_dollars` (not `yes` / `no` as v1 assumed), and each is a list of `[price_string, qty_string]` pairs as STRINGS that need `float()` casting. The v1 probe assumed integer/float primitives and silently summed zero across all markets. **Bug 3 (additive — wasn't a bug, but dropped data):** the per-market list response already contains `yes_bid_dollars`, `yes_ask_dollars`, `no_bid_dollars`, `no_ask_dollars`, `last_price_dollars`, `volume_24h_fp`, `volume_fp`, `open_interest_fp`, `liquidity_dollars`, `yes_bid_size_fp`, `yes_ask_size_fp` — these populate even when the orderbook depth array is empty (top-of-book without queued depth) and are the canonical liquidity signal. The v1 report dropped them despite capturing them upstream. v2 promotes them into the floor-tier table as primary columns. **New parser** `parse_orderbook(ob_response)` walks `ob_response.get("orderbook_fp")`, then iterates `yes_dollars` / `no_dollars` arrays casting each `row[0]` (price) and `row[1]` (qty) through a defensive `_f()` helper that handles None, int, float, or string inputs and returns None on parse failure (skipping that level rather than raising). Returns structured `{yes: {n_levels, total_qty, total_dollar_depth, top_of_book_price, top_of_book_qty}, no: {...}}`. Top-of-book identified as the LAST element (Kalshi sorts ascending by price; LAST is best bid on each side). **New `classify_liquidity()` helper** buckets each market into `liquid` (≥$50 YES depth), `thin` ($5–$50), `top_of_book` (any YES bid > 0 but no/minimal depth), or `empty` (no YES bid). Drives the report's verdict cell. **Same scope as v1** — four NBA player-prop series (`KXNBAPTS`/`KXNBAREB`/`KXNBAAST`/`KXNBA3PT`) × three matchups (DETORL, CLETOR, LALHOU on May 1 slate) × `FLOOR_TIER_COUNT=2` floor-tier definition; the bug was in parsing, not scope. **Pure stdlib only** (no `requests`, no third-party HTTP libraries — `urllib.request`); `THROTTLE_SEC=0.20`, `MAX_PAGES=10`, `PAGE_LIMIT=200` — same polite-throttle posture as v1. **Manual run only — no schedule, no agent integration.** **Verification (all gates pass):** Python `ast.parse` clean; stdlib-only confirmed (only `json`, `time`, `re`, `datetime`, `pathlib`, `urllib`, `zoneinfo`, `__future__`, `collections`); zero NBAgent file mutation patterns; bugfix tokens each appear 4× (`orderbook_fp` = 4, `yes_dollars` = 4, `no_dollars` = 4 — parser + report + tier-ladder mention + dump-key); v1 buggy `ob.get('orderbook')` accessor count = 0 (no fallback to broken path); v1 buggy `.get('yes') or` / `.get('no') or` patterns count = 0 (clean v2 access); both v1 sibling files (`tools/kalshi_reprobe.py` and `tools/kalshi_probe.py`) untouched per `git diff --name-only`. **Files touched:** `tools/kalshi_reprobe_v2.py` (NEW, ~520 lines pure stdlib Python), `data/kalshi_reprobe_v2/` (NEW directory with raw + structured + report artifacts). **Not touched:** `tools/kalshi_reprobe.py` (v1 buggy probe — preserved as historical artifact, broken-script-as-evidence; deliberately keeping the broken script lets future debugging trace which version produced which dataset), `tools/kalshi_probe.py` (broad-discovery probe — preserved), all agents (`auditor`, `analyst`, `build_site`, `parlay`, `quant`, `lineup_update`, `lineup_watch`, `pre_game_reporter`, `post_game_reporter`, `season_context_updater`, `playoff_matchup`, `injury_profiles`), all `ingest/*.py` (FanDuel ingest unaffected — Kalshi remains being PROBED not integrated), all `.github/workflows/*.yml`, all NBAgent `data/*.json` and `data/*.csv` files (probe is read-only against NBAgent state, writes only to new subdirectory), `data/kalshi_probe/` and `data/kalshi_reprobe/` (sister directories from prior probes — left alone), `context/nba_season_context.md`. No CLI flags, no API keys, no auth, GET-only, no order-placement endpoints. No "edge"/"value" comparison vs FanDuel. **The "0 of 355 markets had any depth" finding from v1 is now superseded** — that was a parsing artifact, not a real liquidity signal. v2's classification (liquid / thin / top_of_book / empty) is the canonical answer, with floor-tier vs headline-tier breakdown for the actual decision input. **Recommended downstream work** (queued in `ROADMAP_active.md` under Odds Integration): review `data/kalshi_reprobe_v2/REPORT.md` section 3 (floor-tier liquidity classification). Decision criteria — if ≥30% of floor markets are liquid OR ≥60% have non-empty YES bids, queue offseason `kalshi_today.py` ingest workstream; if <15% are liquid AND <30% have non-empty YES bids, close as "usable for high-volume markets only, insufficient coverage for system-wide use". |
| **Kalshi NBA re-probe (May 1 slate, floor-tier focus, 2026-04-30)** | New targeted discovery script `tools/kalshi_reprobe.py` — companion to the broader `tools/kalshi_probe.py` shipped earlier the same day. Hits ONLY the four NBA player-prop series (`KXNBAPTS`, `KXNBAREB`, `KXNBAAST`, `KXNBA3PT`) on the three matchups for the May 1 slate (DET-ORL, CLE-TOR, LAL-HOU). Hard-coded scope — no keyword filter, no Sports-category enumeration, no fallbacks to wider nets. **Five steps:** (1) `step1_fetch_slate_markets()` queries `/markets?series_ticker=X&status=open` per target series, falls back to bare `status=` if first returns zero, then locally filters by exact `event_ticker == "{series}-{SLATE_DATE_TICKER}{matchup}"` match (no substring matching to avoid cross-matchup contamination). (2) `parse_market()` extracts `(player, tier, prop_type)` from each market via two regexes — one against the ticker suffix `{series}-{YYMMMDD}{TEAM1}{TEAM2}-{TEAM}{LASTNAME}{JERSEY}-{tier}` and one against the title `"<Player>: N+ <unit>"` format — cross-checks tier consistency, surfaces parse warnings on mismatch. (3) `step3_build_tier_ladders()` assembles per-(matchup, player, prop) tier ladder, sorts ascending, marks bottom `FLOOR_TIER_COUNT=2` tiers as "floor tiers" where NBAgent's conservative picks live, marks remainder as "headline tiers". (4) `step4_orderbook_depth()` fetches `/markets/{ticker}/orderbook` for **every** market (not 5 random samples like the broad probe), captures YES/NO bid level counts + total quantity + top bids; defensively handles both `yes`/`no` arrays (cents) and `yes_dollars`/`no_dollars` arrays (dollars) per Kalshi's variable response shape; tags each record with `is_floor_tier` boolean. (5) `step5_write_report()` emits a 7-section `REPORT.md` with explicit FLOOR-TIERS-ONLY orderbook section as the headline finding. **Why floor-tier focus:** NBAgent picks structurally conservative tiers (Marcus Smart PTS T15 not T25; LeBron 3PM T1 not T5) — liquidity at headline markets like "LeBron 5+ threes" is uninformative for our use case. The re-probe explicitly separates floor-tier liquidity (the metric that matters) from headline-tier liquidity (reference only). **Pure stdlib** (no `requests`, no third-party HTTP libraries — `urllib.request` only). Polite throttling (200ms sleep between requests), `MAX_PAGES=10` safety ceiling, `PAGE_LIMIT=200` per-page cap. **Manual run only — no schedule, no agent integration.** **Verification (all gates pass):** Python `ast.parse` clean; stdlib-only confirmed (only `json`, `time`, `re`, `datetime`, `pathlib`, `urllib`, `zoneinfo`, `__future__`, `collections`); zero NBAgent file mutation patterns (`open(.../picks.json|audit_log|audit_summary|player_stats|lineups_today|injuries_today)`); hard-coded scope grep counts — `"KXNBAPTS"` = 2, `"KXNBAREB"` = 2, `"KXNBAAST"` = 2, `"KXNBA3PT"` = 2, `SLATE_MATCHUPS` = 10, `FLOOR_TIER_COUNT` = 5, `is_floor_tier` = 3 (each ≥ spec minimum); no `category.*=.*sports` broad-fallback patterns confirmed (tight scope); date encoding `SLATE_DATE_TICKER = "26MAY01"` matches Kalshi's `YY+MMM+DD` upper-case convention validated against the broad probe's discovered tickers (`KXNBAPTS-26MAY01LALHOU-LALMSMART36-20`, `KXNBA3PT-26MAY01LALHOU-LALLJAMES23-5` etc.). **Files touched:** `tools/kalshi_reprobe.py` (NEW, ~445 lines), `data/kalshi_reprobe/` (NEW directory with raw + structured + report artifacts). **Not touched:** `tools/kalshi_probe.py` (preserved as historical broad-discovery artifact — companion not refactor), all agents (`auditor`, `analyst`, `build_site`, `parlay`, `quant`, `lineup_update`, `lineup_watch`, `pre_game_reporter`, `post_game_reporter`, `season_context_updater`, `playoff_matchup`, `injury_profiles`), all `ingest/*.py` (including `odds_today.py` — Kalshi remains being PROBED not integrated), all `.github/workflows/*.yml` (manual run only), all NBAgent `data/*.json` and `data/*.csv` files (probe is read-only against NBAgent state, writes only to new subdirectory), `data/kalshi_probe/` (sister directory from broad probe — left alone), `context/nba_season_context.md`. No CLI flags, no API key handling, no auth scheme. GET-only — never POSTs, never touches authenticated endpoints. No "edge" or "value" computation between Kalshi prices and FanDuel — strict scope is enumerate-availability-and-shape. No programmatic comparison to NBAgent's `player_dim.csv` or whitelist — cross-reference is a manual review step, not coded. **Recommended downstream work** (queued in `ROADMAP_active.md` under Odds Integration): review `data/kalshi_reprobe/REPORT.md` section 3 (floor-tier orderbook depth). | **Kalshi NBA prop market probe (2026-04-30)** | New read-only discovery script at `tools/kalshi_probe.py`. Hits public Kalshi market-data API (`api.elections.kalshi.com/trade-api/v2/`) **unauthenticated** to enumerate available NBA player prop series, events, markets, and orderbooks. Writes summary report (`REPORT.md`) + raw JSON snapshots (numbered `01_` through `07_`) to a new `data/kalshi_probe/` subdirectory. **Pure stdlib** (no `requests`, no third-party HTTP libraries — `urllib.request` only). Polite throttling (200ms sleep between requests), `MAX_PAGES=10` safety ceiling on cursor pagination, `PAGE_LIMIT=200` per-page cap. **NOT integrated** with any agent or workflow — discovery artifact only. **Five steps:** (1) `step1_find_series()` lists all Sports-category series via `/series?category=Sports`, heuristically filters for NBA / basketball / player-prop keywords; (2) `step2_enumerate_markets()` walks each candidate series via `/events?series_ticker=X&status=open` + `/markets?series_ticker=X&status=open` (with bare `status=` fallback if first call returns zero), tags each market by heuristic title-parsing into PTS / REB / AST / 3PM / OTHER prop bucket; (3) `step3_orderbook_sample()` samples up to 5 markets across candidate series and fetches `/markets/{ticker}/orderbook` to compute YES/NO bid level counts + total quantity; (4) `step4_deep_dive()` picks the highest-volume market across all candidates and fetches full event detail + market detail + orderbook for one concrete example; (5) `step5_write_report()` emits a 7-section Markdown report at `data/kalshi_probe/REPORT.md` answering the seven probe questions (which series tickers, which props, how many markets, tier/threshold structure, orderbook depth, implied prob format, settlement rules). **Wide-net fallback** in `main()` — if the Sports-category search returns zero NBA candidates, automatically widens to ALL series across all categories and re-filters. **First run on 2026-04-30:** Sports-category enumeration returned the full Sports universe and the NBA-keyword filter matched 250+ candidate series (intentionally broad — also catches WNBA, CBA, EuroCup, college basketball, "points" sports of any kind). cross-market analysis is offseason scope. **Recommended downstream work** (queued in `ROADMAP_active.md` under Odds Integration): review `data/kalshi_probe/REPORT.md` to determine offseason scope. Decision points: (a) does Kalshi offer alternate tier markets (T15, T20, T25, T30 for PTS) or only consensus lines; (b) is orderbook liquidity sufficient for implied probabilities to be meaningful; (c) what's the player coverage overlap with our active whitelist; (d) does Kalshi's settlement match FanDuel's HIT/MISS at the same threshold (overtime, voided games, DNPs). If answers favor integration, queue an offseason workstream: `kalshi_today.py` ingest mirror + per-pick `kalshi_implied_prob` field + cross-market disagreement-as-signal hypothesis (potential H35). If answers don't favor integration (thin liquidity, narrow coverage, divergent settlement rules), close as "Kalshi prop markets exist but don't add NBAgent value at current scale". |

The warning is a separate `clv_warning` sub-object — does NOT compete with the auditor's authoritative `clv_pp` field. **Filter (all 5 conditions must hold to fire):** `prop_type in CLV_WARN_PROP_TYPES` (set to `{"AST"}` only — H34 cross-prop reference cells confirmed PTS/REB/3PM × lost_close show no comparable degradation, +1.2pp/-2.0pp/+2.5pp respectively); `morning_implied_prob` and `market_implied_prob` both not None; `live_clv_pp < -0.5`; `voided is not True`; `result not in ("HIT", "MISS")` (don't add pretip warning to a settled pick). **`clv_warning` schema:** `{type: "ast_lost_close", live_clv_pp, morning_implied_prob (1dp), market_implied_prob (1dp), threshold: -0.5, proposed_penalty_pp: 5, applied: false (always), first_observed_at (sticky), last_observed_at (refreshed each cycle), source_backtest: "H34 — backtest_clv_ast_disagree (2026-04-30)"}`. **Idempotency + recovery semantics:** re-running on the same picks refreshes `live_clv_pp` and `last_observed_at` while preserving `first_observed_at` from the first observation (sticky). | **CLV multi-dimensional analysis tool (2026-04-30)** | New read-only utility at `tools/clv_analysis.py` decomposes Closing Line Value across five dimensions: (1) prop type (PTS/REB/AST/3PM); (2) confidence band (70-75/76-80/81-85/86+); (3) CLV magnitude bucket (no_move ≤0.5pp / small 0.5–2.0 / medium 2.0–5.0 / large >5.0) with directional sub-splits (small_beat / small_lost / medium_beat / medium_lost / large_beat / large_lost); (4) miss classification co-occurrence (groups misses by `miss_classification` field, computes within-group beat%/lost%/no_move% — answers e.g. "are injury_event misses dominated by lost_close?"); (5) per-player rollup with top-10 / bottom-10 by avg_clv_pp (min 5 picks). Output: `data/clv_analysis_YYYY-MM-DD.md` Markdown report. Reads `picks.json` directly using the same filter as `auditor.py:1485-1488` (`clv_pp` is not None AND `result in ("HIT", "MISS")` AND `voided is not True`) so headline rollup is byte-identical to `audit_summary.json.clv_summary`. **Pure stdlib only** (no pandas, no numpy) per spec — single-file standalone script ~430 lines, single entry point `main()`, no CLI flags, no mutations, idempotent. **First run on 2026-04-30 against 407 CLV-qualified picks** (out of 1310 total in `picks.json`, 31.1% coverage rate, 2 voided picks defensively excluded). Headline reproduces audit_summary exactly: `avg_clv_pp = +0.05pp`, beat_close = 109 (26.8%, 83.5% hit rate), lost_close = 101 (24.8%, 81.2% hit rate), no_movement = 197 (48.4%, 89.3% hit rate). **Sample-of-many findings surfaced by the breakdowns** (interpretation deferred to Oliver — tool is descriptive, not prescriptive): (a) prop-type variance — REB has slightly negative avg_clv (-0.10pp) and 3PM has the largest positive avg_clv (+0.43pp); AST shows the strongest market signal asymmetry with `lost_close` AST hitting only 62.5% vs `beat_close` AST at 84.4% (∆ = +21.9pp). (b) confidence band — beat_close hit rate is U-shaped across bands (77.8% at 70-75, jumps to 93.9% at 76-80, then thins out at higher bands due to small samples). (c) magnitude — `medium_lost` (clv ∈ [-5.0, -2.0]) is the highest-hit-rate sub-bucket at 92.0% (n=25), and `large_lost` (clv < -5.0) drops to 71.4% (n=7) — suggests modest line movement against us is noise but large adverse movement carries real signal. (d) miss classification — 58 of 58 misses currently land in `unclassified` because `miss_classification` is not yet wired onto pick records; tool handles this gracefully and surfaces it as the only row in Breakdown 4 (auditor writes the field on miss_details inside audit_log entries but does not mirror it onto the underlying pick dicts; future enhancement). (e) per-player — top-of-leaderboard is Jabari Smith Jr. (+2.48pp avg_clv, 100% hit rate over 10 picks) and Amen Thompson (+1.54pp, 100% over 16 picks) — both could be flagged as "market consistently undervalues these players going into tip" if the pattern holds across more samples. **Verification (all gates pass):** Python `ast.parse` clean; helper imports cleanly (`from tools.clv_analysis import rollup_cell, is_clv_pick, magnitude_bucket`); banned-imports check confirms no pandas/numpy; mutation check confirms no `open(PICKS_JSON, "w"|"a")` calls; tool runs cleanly producing the report file; headline numbers match `audit_summary.json.clv_summary` byte-identical (n=407 / +0.05 / beat 109 83.5% / lost 101 81.2% / no_move 197 89.3%); 5 logical invariants pass — prop-type rows sum to 407, confidence-band rows + 3 excluded sum to 407, magnitude buckets sum to 407, no_move bucket = headline.no_movement (197 = 197), miss-class total n_misses = headline misses (58 = 58); all 5 breakdown sections present in markdown output (`## Breakdown 1:` through `## Breakdown 5:`). **Files touched:** `tools/clv_analysis.py` (NEW, ~430 lines stdlib), `data/clv_analysis_2026-04-30.md` (NEW, output — overwritten on re-run with same date). **Not touched:** `agents/auditor.py` (auditor's CLV computation is the source of truth — tool is a downstream consumer), `agents/analyst.py`, `agents/build_site.py`, `agents/parlay.py`, `agents/quant.py`, all other agents, `audit_summary.json` or any other `data/*.json`/`data/*.csv` (read-only — `picks.json` and `audit_summary.json` both untouched), all `ingest/*.py`, all `.github/workflows/*.yml` (no schedule needed — manual one-off), `context/nba_season_context.md`. **No backtest mode** added to `agents/backtest.py` per spec — this is descriptive, not a hypothesis test. **No CLI flags** per spec — single entry point, no parameters. **No CLV references** added to any prompt-construction code — read-only analysis. **Recommended downstream work** (offseason or follow-up task — queued in `ROADMAP_active.md`): decide based on the breakdowns whether to (a) build an Audit Log CLV panel surfacing the headline + magnitude split for daily situational awareness; (b) add a pre-tip caution layer when `market_implied_prob` drops materially vs `morning_implied_prob` (the `medium_lost` 92.0% finding contradicts naive intuition that lost_close = bad pick); (c) feed CLV-conditional hit rates into the analyst rolling performance summary; | **Auto-trim engine playoff gate (2026-04-30)** | Stage-3 Review API call in `agents/analyst.py main()` now skipped when `is_playoff_mode()` returns True (`data/playoff_matchup.json` exists with `mode=="playoffs"` and `date==TODAY_STR`). **Empirical motivation:** observed ~95% false-positive rate on Review's `concern`/`stay_away` flags across multiple playoff slates. 4/28: 8 of 9 review-flagged picks false-positive (clean picks tagged manual_skip on regular-season-derived warnings that do not transfer to playoff series). 4/30: 13 of 13 review-flagged picks false-positive on a 33-pick slate, producing a 39% flag rate against the agent's own documented 17–33% target. Root cause: Review reasons from regular-season-derived signals (FG_COLD, FG_MARGIN_NEG, raw_avg comparisons, post-miss bounce-back, volatile tag) that are empirically dominated by playoff series tier hit rates the agent does not know to weight differently — a player with 70%+ tier hit rate over the last 4 series games will still be flagged as fragile by Review on the basis of a regular-season FG_COLD or VOLATILE annotation. Recalibrating the Review prompt mid-postseason was rejected as too risky; gating the call off until regular season returns is the surgical fix. **Implementation:** two surgical edits to `agents/analyst.py` only. Returns `False` on any failure path (missing file, parse error, stale date, mode mismatch) — fail-open default ensures regular-season behavior is preserved when the gate cannot positively confirm playoffs. Helper does NOT print on failure paths (those are already noisy from `load_series_context()`'s own logging); the decision-time print happens in `main()` to document whether Review was skipped or run. (2) New `elif is_playoff_mode():` branch inserted in the Stage-3 Review block (line 6351) between the existing `if not picks:` early-skip and the original `else:` body, with a 5-line preamble comment explaining the gate's motivation and reversal path. | **Auditor recommendation contamination guards (2026-04-30)** | The 2026-04-29 audit produced 5 recommendations, 3 of which were contaminated: Rec #3 (Mobley dossier CAUTION at lower tiers) was derived from a `variance`-classified miss — a pick the auditor itself classified as "within normal variance range" was used to motivate tightening; Rec #4 (LATE_FADER + VOLATILE skip rule for Mobley PTS, Harden PTS) was derived from picks that **HIT** at 68% confidence — tightening based on uncomfortable-but-correct hits is overfitting to noise that didn't even occur; Rec #5 (Ingram-type 3+ structural warnings as skip-eligible) was derived from an `injury_event` miss (Ingram exited at 11 minutes with heel inflammation) — the existing injury guardrail at line 1123 explicitly said "Do NOT write a lesson or recommendation" but the auditor wrote one anyway by reframing the rec around the *risk profile* (FG_COLD + VOLATILE + 70% confidence) rather than the injury miss itself. Contaminated recommendations roll up into `audit_summary.json.recent_recommendations` and feed the Analyst's ROLLING PERFORMANCE SUMMARY on the next run, directly causing the Analyst to tighten on noise. **Fix:** strengthened and expanded the existing recommendation guardrail block in `agents/auditor.py` from 7 lines to ~95 lines via a single targeted Edit. The block at line 1123 was replaced with a new `IMPORTANT — RECOMMENDATION CONTAMINATION GUARDS:` block organized around three explicit guards plus an informational note plus an explicit allowlist summary. **GUARD 1 — INJURY AND WORKFLOW MISSES** preserves the original guidance verbatim and adds an explicit anti-bypass clause: "This guard cannot be bypassed by reframing the recommendation around the pick's risk profile … the risk profile that 'would have been fragile if the player had actually played' is not evidence — the player did not play long enough to test the profile." Cites the FG_COLD + VOLATILE + 70% Ingram framing pattern as the canonical bypass to forbid. **GUARD 2 — VARIANCE MISSES** is new: lessons may describe a variance miss for context but the lessons array entry must NOT propose a rule change, and the recommendations array must NOT contain any rule motivated by a variance-classified pick. Captures the bright line "Lessons describe; recommendations prescribe. Variance can drive a description but never a prescription." Directly blocks the Mobley AST T2 rec #3 pattern. **GUARD 3 — HITS** is new: the recommendations array exists exclusively to address actual MISSES — a pick that HIT, regardless of how marginally or how uncomfortable the auditor felt about it, may NOT motivate a tightening recommendation. Provides the redirect path: pattern observations on marginal hits belong in the reinforcements array ("the minimum confidence floor is calibrated correctly for these cases"), not the recommendations array. Directly blocks the Mobley + Harden PTS T10 rec #4 pattern. **NARROW MISS NOTE** (informational, not a hard guard): clarifies that a miss by exactly 1 unit on PTS/REB/AST should default to variance classification absent a specific structural mechanism (e.g. "no T10 market existed; inability to step down materially raised tail risk" or "opponent's league-leading OREB% structurally compresses opponent REB volume"). Prevents future drift toward classifying every miss-by-1 as `model_gap` on "system should have been more cautious" reasoning, which by construction would tighten the system into producing zero picks. **SUMMARY OF WHAT IS ALLOWED** explicitly enumerates the four legitimate recommendation drivers: selection_error misses, model_gap_rule with explicit reproducible mechanism, model_gap_signal with identifiable missing signal, or patterns of repeated misses across multiple picks revealing a systematic blind spot. Closes with the explicit fallback: "If the slate had no qualifying misses for recommendations, write recommendations addressing reinforcements … An empty or short recommendations array is preferable to a contaminated one." **Verification (all 6 gates pass):** Python `ast.parse` clean on `agents/auditor.py`; full module imports cleanly via stub-anthropic test (`import agents.auditor`); spec-grep matrix passes — old `IMPORTANT — INJURY AND WORKFLOW MISSES:` anchor count = 0 (replaced), new `RECOMMENDATION CONTAMINATION GUARDS:` anchor = 1, `GUARD 1 — INJURY AND WORKFLOW MISSES:` = 1, `GUARD 2 — VARIANCE MISSES:` = 1, `GUARD 3 — HITS:` = 1, old trailing phrase `they must not pollute the Analyst's feedback loop` = 0. **Files touched:** `agents/auditor.py` only — single Edit replaces the 7-line block at line 1123 with the ~95-line expansion. Pure prompt-text change inside the f-string that builds the auditor's prompt; no Python logic changes, no schema changes, no f-string brace-escaping issues. **Not touched:** the recommendation generation count instruction at line ~1154 ("Synthesize 3-5 concrete, actionable recommendations") — the new guards explicitly allow short or empty recommendation arrays as preferable to contaminated ones, but the upstream instruction remains so the LLM still aims for 3-5 by default; OUTPUT FORMAT JSON schema at line ~1158; any other STEP block (STEP 0–6); `recent_recommendations` roll-up logic at line ~1411 (filtering happens at write time via auditor LLM compliance, not at roll-up time); `agents/analyst.py`, `agents/quant.py`, `agents/parlay.py`, `agents/backtest.py`, `agents/build_site.py`, `agents/lineup_watch.py`, `agents/lineup_update.py`, `agents/pre_game_reporter.py`, `agents/post_game_reporter.py`, `agents/playoff_matchup.py`, `agents/season_context_updater.py`, `agents/injury_profiles.py`, all `ingest/*.py`, all `.github/workflows/*.yml`, all data files, `context/nba_season_context.md`. **Existing audit_log entries NOT backfilled** — contamination in past entries (notably 2026-04-29's recs 3, 4, 5) naturally rolls off the 5-day `recent_recommendations` window in `audit_summary.json` over the next 5 audit runs without retroactive cleanup. **Empirical motivation:** 2026-04-29 was the first observed instance where contaminated recommendations explicitly bypassed an existing guardrail by reframing — the FG_COLD + VOLATILE + 70% Ingram framing was structurally a recommendation about the analyst's selection logic but was packaged as if it were about the post-injury risk profile. The strengthened block names this exact bypass pattern and forbids it. **Production verification deferred** — the 2026-04-30 auditor run will use the strengthened prompt; subsequent reports should contain no recommendations derived from injury_event misses, workflow_gap misses, variance-classified misses, or hits. **Escalation path** if behavioral instruction proves unreliable across multiple runs: Python-side filter at `recent_recommendations` roll-up (line ~1411), which would require structured tagging on each recommendation by miss source — a larger change deferred unless and until contamination recurs despite verbatim guardrail text. |
| **Analyst observability — penalty cap + walk decision telemetry (2026-04-30)** | Added passive observability for two structural rules in `agents/analyst.py` — the PENALTY STACK LIMIT MAGNITUDE CAP rule (landed 2026-04-28) and the TIER_WALK MARKET-AWARENESS rule (landed 2026-04-26 as Layer A LLM rule + Layer B Python `revert_no_market_walk` post-processor). **Problem:** both rules currently produce observable output ONLY when they fire. The 2026-04-28 verification sweep confirmed this: zero `[WALK_REVERTED:` annotations across 85 picks 4/26-4/28, and zero `PENALTY_CAP applied` annotations on the 4/28 slate. Cannot distinguish "rule fired correctly" from "rule was bypassed silently" from "no trigger condition occurred." Time-to-evidence unbounded — both fixes were shipped to address rare-but-consequential failures (LeBron silent rejection 4/26, Jokic AST T8 silent skip 4/27); waiting for natural recurrence to confirm they work is acceptable but not ideal heading into R2. **Fix:** added two parallel observability layers. **(1) RAW PENALTY ANNOTATION sub-rule** added to PENALTY STACK LIMIT block in both `build_prompt()` and `build_pick_prompt()` via `replace_all=true` (single Edit hits both byte-identical occurrences). The new sub-rule sits inside the MAGNITUDE CAP block immediately after the HOW TO APPLY THE CAP block and before INTERACTION WITH COUNT RULE. Instructs the LLM to emit `[PENALTY_RAW: <value>pp]` annotation on every pick where at least one penalty applies, BEFORE the magnitude cap or any floor check. The annotation captures the SIGNED aggregate sum of penalties (e.g. `[PENALTY_RAW: -8pp]`, `[PENALTY_RAW: -25pp]`). When the cap fires, the existing `[PENALTY_CAP applied: ...]` annotation follows on the next line. Picks without any penalty (clean iron_floor picks) do not need this annotation. Format examples preserved verbatim from spec. **(2) WALK DECLINED ANNOTATION sub-rule** added to TIER_WALK MARKET-AWARENESS bullet in SELECTION RULES of both prompts via `replace_all=true`. Sits immediately after the existing rule text (ending "safety, not market evasion.") and before the `CRITICAL — pick_value + walked_tier output contract` bullet. Instructs the LLM to emit `[WALK_DECLINED: T<from>→T<to>, no market]` whenever it declines a tier walk because the target tier has no FanDuel market. This is the LLM-side counterpart to Layer B's existing `[WALK_REVERTED:` Python annotation — together they cover both Layer A (LLM-prevented) and Layer B (Python-rescued) cases. **(3) Python observability post-processor** — four new functions added immediately above `save_picks()`: `_parse_penalty_observability(pick)` regex-extracts raw_pp + cap_applied + savings_pp from tier_walk text (returns None when no penalty annotation present); `_parse_walk_observability(pick)` extracts walk decline/revert outcome (returns None for normal walks); `_log_observability(pick)` emits per-pick `[analyst] OBS PENALTY:` and `[analyst] OBS WALK_*:` console log lines visible in analyst.yml workflow output; `compute_observability(picks)` orchestrator iterates picks and writes `obs_penalty` and `obs_walk` sub-objects to each pick dict. Module-level regex compilation via `import re as _re_obs` alias to avoid shadowing the existing in-function `import re` patterns. Regexes accept either Unicode `→` or ASCII `->` arrow. Cap-fired-without-raw fallback: if `[PENALTY_CAP applied:]` is present but `[PENALTY_RAW:]` was omitted by the LLM, raw_pp is inferred from the cap annotation's first capture group (graceful LLM-omission handling). **(4) save_picks chain insertion** — `compute_observability(picks)` inserted as final step in the `save_picks()` chain, after `enforce_market_gate(picks)` and before the file-load/append/write block. Order is deliberate: picks filtered or rejected upstream do not appear at observability time, all upstream mutations (Layer B revert, game attribution corrections) are already applied to tier_walk so observability sees the final state, and observability is a pure read of tier_walk text — does not mutate any existing field, only adds new top-level keys to each pick dict. **Schema:** picks.json gets two new top-level keys per pick: `obs_penalty` (`{raw_pp, cap_applied, savings_pp}` or `None`) and `obs_walk` (`{outcome, from_tier, to_tier}` or `None`). Both keys additive; auditor / build_site / lineup_watch / lineup_update consumers ignore unknown keys. The `obs_walk.outcome` enum is intentionally narrow ("declined", "reverted", or absent) — only the two interesting walk events are telemetried; normal walks to market-supported tiers are inferable from `pick_value` vs `best_tier` post-hoc and don't need their own field. **Verification (all gates pass):** Python `ast.parse` clean; spec-grep matrix passes (RAW PENALTY ANNOTATION = 2, WALK DECLINED ANNOTATION = 2, def compute_observability = 1, def _parse_penalty_observability = 1, def _parse_walk_observability = 1, def _log_observability = 1, single `picks = compute_observability(picks)` call site in save_picks chain); 4 self-checks all pass — (a) function imports cleanly via `from agents.analyst import compute_observability, _parse_penalty_observability, _parse_walk_observability`; (b) parser tests on 6 synthetic cases all return expected values (raw-only, raw+cap, no-penalty, walk-declined, walk-reverted, normal-pick); (c) orchestrator end-to-end produces correct obs_penalty and obs_walk values + console log lines in `[analyst] OBS PENALTY: <name> <prop> T<tier> raw=<value>pp [CAP_APPLIED]` format; (d) idempotency confirmed — calling `compute_observability(picks)` twice produces identical results, function reads tier_walk and never mutates it. **Production effect:** every analyst run from this point forward produces measurable evidence about both rules' decision distributions, even when neither rule mutates a pick. After 5–10 days of accumulation, will have data to confirm whether Layer A is preventing trigger conditions (would see WALK_DECLINED entries) or whether trigger conditions just aren't arising naturally (would see all clean walks). Affected: `agents/analyst.py` only. **Not touched:** `filter_self_skip_picks`, `reconcile_pick_values`, `revert_no_market_walk`, `reconcile_game_attribution`, `enforce_market_gate` (observability sits AFTER these, doesn't replace any), existing `[PENALTY_CAP applied:]` LLM annotation rule (kept intact, new `[PENALTY_RAW:]` rule sits ALONGSIDE), existing `[WALK_REVERTED:` Python annotation in `revert_no_market_walk` (parsed but unchanged), `save_picks()` signature, `MIN_GAMES`/`PLAYER_WINDOW` constants, `agents/auditor.py` (will not consume new fields — separate future task), `agents/build_site.py` (will not render new fields — diagnostic data, not user-facing), all other agent files, all `ingest/*.py`, all `.github/workflows/*.yml`, all data files, `context/nba_season_context.md`. **Recommended downstream work** (offseason or follow-up task): consume `obs_penalty` distribution in `audit_summary.json` to surface penalty-incidence and cap-fire-rate metrics; surface `obs_walk` declined/reverted ratio as a Layer A vs Layer B effectiveness check. **Companion telemetry:** complements the existing `MARKET_GATE_REJECT` log (Layer B safety net) and the recently-shipped `compute_minutes_floor()` filter (2026-04-28) which together form the observability + correctness pair for the analyst's structural rules going into R2. |
| **`compute_minutes_floor()` — exclude injury exits and anomalously-low-minute games (2026-04-28)** | Fixed bug in `agents/quant.py` `compute_minutes_floor()` where the L10 minutes percentile calculation included injury-exit games (e.g., 12-minute concussion exits), contaminating the floor and cascading into false skips downstream in the Analyst's `min_floor` rule. **Canonical case:** Wembanyama on the 2026-04-28 slate auto manual_skipped on PTS T15 because his `floor_minutes` was 15.6 (driven by his 12-min G2 concussion exit vs POR on 2026-04-21) against `avg_minutes` of 27.9. G4 return showed 34 min with no restriction — the floor was misleading, not a real signal. **Fix:** before computing the 10th percentile and mean, filter L10 minutes to a qualifying set where `minutes >= max(15.0, 0.5 * median(L10_minutes))`. The absolute 15.0 catches injury exits (almost always <15 min); the 0.5 * median is a relative backstop for high-minute players. Both `floor_minutes` and `avg_minutes` are now computed on the filtered set (consistent semantics — both fields describe "what this player does when they meaningfully play"). The same `MIN_GAMES` (5) graceful-null floor applies to the qualifying count, so a player whose recent log is dominated by injury-affected games receives `None` rather than a misleading floor. **Schema and field names unchanged:** returns `{floor_minutes, avg_minutes, n}` or `None` exactly as before — downstream consumers (player profile narrative builder at `quant.py` line ~2669, analyst `min_floor_str` annotation) read those exact keys. **Self-checks pass (synthetic):** (a) one 12-min injury exit in L10 of [12, 25, 26, 28, 29, 30, 31, 32, 33, 35] correctly excludes the 12 (median=29.5, qualifying_min=15) → `n=9, floor=25.8, avg=29.9`; (b) clean L10 of [25–35] passes through unchanged → `n=10, floor=25.9, avg=29.6`; (c) injury-dominated L10 of [10, 11, 12, 13, 14, 14.5, 28, 30, 32, 34] (median=14.25, qualifying_min=15) yields only 4 qualifying games → returns `None` correctly. Python `ast.parse` clean. **Files:** `agents/quant.py` only — body and docstring of `compute_minutes_floor()`. **Not touched:** function signature, return schema, `MIN_GAMES`/`PLAYER_WINDOW` constants, sort direction or `.head(window)` pattern, DNP defensive filter, any other function in `quant.py`, `agents/analyst.py` (same field names, same return schema, restored semantic — no consumer changes needed), `agents/auditor.py`, `agents/parlay.py`, `agents/backtest.py`, `agents/build_site.py`, `agents/lineup_watch.py`, `agents/lineup_update.py`, `agents/pre_game_reporter.py`, `agents/post_game_reporter.py`, `agents/playoff_matchup.py`, `agents/season_context_updater.py`, `agents/injury_profiles.py`, all `ingest/*.py`, all `.github/workflows/*.yml`, all data files, `context/nba_season_context.md`. **Production verification deferred** — user will run quant manually after the edit lands and inspect `data/player_stats.json` (Wembanyama's `floor_minutes` should recompute from 15.6 to a high-20s value reflecting his typical full-game minutes; healthy-log players like Brunson/Jokic/SGA should be substantially unchanged). |
| **Penalty cap rule shipped (2026-04-28)** | Added MAGNITUDE CAP rule to `agents/analyst.py:build_prompt()` and `build_pick_prompt()` PENALTY STACK LIMIT section (single `replace_all=true` Edit hitting both occurrences of the byte-identical 6-line block). Caps the aggregate magnitude of stacked confidence penalties at -20pp regardless of how many individual penalties applied. Parallel to (does not replace) the existing COUNT rule which catches >3 penalties. The block is now structured as `PENALTY STACK LIMIT — TWO PARALLEL CONSTRAINTS:` with `1. COUNT LIMIT` (existing rule preserved verbatim under heading) and `2. MAGNITUDE CAP` (new rule with full reasoning, application instructions, and interaction notes). Each rule addresses a different failure mode: COUNT catches discipline failures (penalty redundancy / weak justification), MAGNITUDE catches over-stacking where each penalty is individually defensible but the aggregate over-penalizes structurally strong picks. **Canonical case:** 2026-04-27 Jokic AST T8 — base 90%, VOLATILE -8% + MIN×AST suppressor -12% + blowout -5% = -25pp aggregate → 65% confidence → silently skipped via `merit_below_floor` (below 68% AST floor). Actual outcome: 16-AST triple-double in DEN's must-win G5. Pick was empirically near-certain, not marginal. Each penalty was individually defensible but the aggregate was wrong by ~25pp. With the cap, aggregate is capped at -20pp → 70% final confidence (above 68% floor) → pick ships → captures the hit. The new rule includes detailed application guidance: document each penalty individually, document the cap explicitly via `PENALTY_CAP applied: -Xpp aggregate exceeds -20pp limit, capping at -20pp` annotation in tier_walk, apply the capped adjustment (-20pp) rather than the uncapped sum. The cap does NOT change which penalties applied — all individual penalties remain documented and visible in tier_walk; only the aggregate effect on final confidence is capped. **Interaction rules in the prompt:** (a) COUNT rule still fires independently — if 4+ penalties AND magnitude exceeds -20pp, COUNT directs re-examine first, may reduce magnitude below cap threshold without invoking it; (b) FLOOR check still applies after the cap — cap raises confidence by 0-5pp depending on excess, which may push borderline picks above the prop-type minimum floor (PTS/AST 68%, REB 78%, 3PM 75%), but capped picks still below floor still skip via `merit_below_floor` (cap does not override floor); (c) POSITIVE-SIGNAL OFFSETS (iron_floor, consistent, soft DvP, favorable rest) apply BEFORE the cap is computed, so strong positive context can keep a pick below the cap threshold without invoking it. Scout untouched per project convention (rules-free; doesn't perform penalty arithmetic). Fix is prompt-text only — no Python post-processor (penalty math is too LLM-internal for clean post-processing; parsing penalty values from natural-language tier_walk text would be fragile). This is intentionally different from the home/away (2026-04-25) and tier-walk-market-aware (2026-04-26) fixes which had Python post-processors — penalty math is too internal to LLM reasoning to admit clean post-processing. Cap value (-20pp) is empirically calibrated: -20pp on 90% base lands at 70% (above all prop floors); on 80% base lands at 60% (below all floors, picks correctly skip). Preserves the meritorious-skip distinction while preventing over-stacking false skips. Affected: `agents/analyst.py`. **Not touched:** any other agent file, any data file, any Python function in `analyst.py` (prompt-text-only fix), `build_scout_prompt()`, individual penalty values (VOLATILE -5%, FG_MARGIN_THIN -2%, etc. all unchanged — cap is a parallel constraint, not a recalibration), prop-type minimum floors (still 68%/68%/78%/75%), positive-signal offset rules, all `ingest/*.py`, all `.github/workflows/*.yml`, `context/nba_season_context.md`. **Verification (all gates pass):** Python `ast.parse` clean; spec-grep matrix passes (PENALTY STACK LIMIT — TWO PARALLEL CONSTRAINTS = 2, MAGNITUDE CAP = 4 references across both prompts, PENALTY_CAP applied = 2, Jokic AST T8 = 4, 16-AST triple-double = 2, 1. COUNT LIMIT = 2, 2.
